The City of Charleston, South Carolina, Waterworks and Sewer System Capital Improvement Revenue Bonds, Series 2022 (the “Series 2022 Bonds”) 
will initially be issued to and registered only in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee for The Depository Trust Company, New York, New York (“DTC”), which 
will act as securities depository for the Series 2022 Bonds.  The Series 2022 Bonds will be available to purchasers under the book-entry only system maintained 
by DTC through brokers and dealers who are, or act through, DTC Participants.  Purchasers will not be entitled to receive physical delivery of the Series 2022 
Bonds.  For so long as any purchaser is the beneficial owner of a Series 2022 Bond, such purchaser must maintain an account with a broker or dealer who 
is, or acts through, a DTC Participant in order to receive payment of principal of and interest on such Bond.  See “DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2022 
BONDS -- Book Entry Only System” herein.
The Series 2022 Bonds are issuable as fully registered bonds in denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof and are interchangeable as 
provided in the Bond Ordinance (as defined herein).  Except as otherwise described herein, interest on the Series 2022 Bonds (payable semi-annually on 
each January 1 and July 1, commencing January  1, 2023) is payable by payment to DTC or its nominee as the registered owner of the Series 2022 Bonds.  
Disbursements of payments of interest and of principal to DTC Participants is the responsibility of DTC, and disbursement of such payments to the owners of 
book-entry interests is the responsibility of DTC Participants and Indirect Participants, as more fully described herein.
The Series 2022 Bonds are subject to optional and mandatory redemption prior to maturity as described herein.
The Series 2022 Bonds are being issued (i)  to finance a portion of the costs of certain capital improvements to the waterworks and sewer system (the 
“System”) of the City of Charleston, South Carolina (the “City”); and (ii) to pay capitalized interest on the Series 2022 Bonds through July 1, 2023.  
The Series 2022 Bonds are payable from gross revenues of the System which remain after paying operation and maintenance costs of the System and will 
be issued on a parity with the outstanding waterworks and sewer system revenue bonds of the City as further described herein.
THE SERIES 2022 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE AN INDEBTEDNESS OF THE CITY OF CHARLESTON WITHIN THE MEANING OF 
ANY PROVISION, LIMITATION OR RESTRICTION OF THE CONSTITUTION OR THE LAWS OF THE STATE OF SOUTH CAROLINA, OTHER 
THAN THOSE PROVISIONS AUTHORIZING INDEBTEDNESS PAYABLE SOLELY FROM A REVENUE-PRODUCING PROJECT NOT INVOLVING 
REVENUES FROM ANY TAX OR LICENSE.  THE CITY IS NOT OBLIGATED TO PAY ANY OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS OR THE INTEREST 
THEREON EXCEPT FROM REVENUES DERIVED FROM THE OPERATION OF THE SYSTEM.  NO RECOURSE MAY BE HAD FOR THE PAYMENT 
OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS AGAINST THE GENERAL FUND OF THE CITY , AND NEITHER THE FULL FAITH AND CREDIT NOR THE TAXING 
POWER OF THE CITY SHALL BE DEEMED PLEDGED TO THE PAYMENT OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS.

OFFICIAL STATEMENT 
$151,190,000 
CITY OF CHARLESTON, SOUTH CAROLINA 
Waterworks and Sewer System  
Capital Improvement Revenue Bonds 
Series 2022 
INTRODUCTION 
This Official Statement, which includes the cover page hereof, the Table of Contents and the Appendices 
hereto, is provided to furnish certain information in connection with the offer of $151,190,000 principal amount of 
Waterworks and Sewer System Capital Improvement Revenue Bonds, Series 2022 (the "Series 2022 Bonds") to be 
issued by the City of Charleston, South Carolina (the "City" or "Charleston"). 
The Series 2022 Bonds will be issued pursuant to, and in accordance with, Chapter 17 of Title 6 of the 
Code of Laws of South Carolina 1976, as amended, as well as other applicable laws (collectively, the "Act"), an 
ordinance enacted by the City Council of the City of Charleston (the "City Council") on October 24, 1984 (as 
amended, the "Bond Ordinance"), a series ordinance enacted by the City Council on May 24, 2022 (the "2022 Series 
Ordinance") and a resolution adopted by the Commissioners of Public Works of the City of Charleston (the 
"Commissioners" or "CPW") on May 24, 2022 (the "Resolution").  The Bond Ordinance is more particularly 
described in Appendix C - "SUMMARY OF BOND ORDINANCE". 
The Series 2022 Bonds are being issued (i) to finance a portion of the costs of certain capital improvements 
(collectively, the "Projects") to the waterworks and sewer system (the "System") of the City; and (ii) to pay 
capitalized interest on the Series 2022 Bonds through July 1, 2023.   
All information included herein has been provided by the Commissioners except where attributed to other 
sources.  The summaries and references to all documents, statutes, reports and other instruments referred to herein 
do not purport to be complete, comprehensive or definitive, and each such reference or summary is qualified in its 
entirety by reference to each such document, statute, report or other instrument. 
DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS 
Terms and Form 
The Series 2022 Bonds will be issued as fully-registered bonds, without coupons, in denominations of 
$5,000 or any integral multiple thereof.  The Series 2022 Bonds will be dated the date of their delivery, will mature 
on January 1 in the years and in the principal amounts set forth on the cover page hereof, and will bear interest at the 
rates per annum set forth on the cover page hereof payable on January 1, 2023, and semiannually thereafter on 
January 1 and July 1 of each year.  The Series 2022 Bonds will initially be issued solely in book-entry form.  (See 
"Book-Entry-Only System" below.)  In the event that the Series 2022 Bonds are no longer held in a book-entry only 
system, the principal of the Series 2022 Bonds will be payable at the corporate trust office of The Bank of New 
York Mellon Trust Company, N.A. (the "Trustee"), as trustee, registrar and paying agent, and interest on the Series 
2022 Bonds will be paid by check or draft mailed by the Trustee, as paying agent, to the registered owner thereof as 
shown on the registration books on the 15th day of the month prior to each interest payment date. 
Redemption 
Optional Redemption.  The Series 2022 Bonds maturing on or after January 1, 2033 are subject to 
redemption prior to maturity at the option of the City on or after July 1, 2032 as a whole or in part at any time at the 
redemption price of par, together with accrued interest to the redemption date.  If less than all of the Series 2022 
Bonds are to be redeemed, such Series 2022 Bonds shall be redeemed in such order of their maturities as shall be 
determined by the Commissioners, and by lot selected by the Trustee within a maturity. 2 
Mandatory Sinking Fund Redemption.  The Series 2022 Bonds maturing on January 1, 2047 are subject to 
mandatory sinking fund redemption prior to maturity in part by lot on each January 1 in the years and in the 
principal amounts shown below and shall be redeemed (to the extent not previously redeemed) at 100% of the 
principal amount plus accrued interest to the redemption date:

redeemed (to the extent not previously redeemed) at 100% of the principal amount plus accrued interest to the

The amount of the mandatory sinking fund redemption prescribed above for the Series 2022 Bonds of any 
maturity shall be reduced to the extent Series 2022 Bonds of such maturity have been purchased by the Commissioners 
or redeemed by the Commissioners pursuant to the optional redemption provisions set forth above, in such manner as 
the Commissioners shall direct, or, absent such direction, on a pro rata basis. 
Notice of Redemption 
Notice of redemption shall be given by mailing a copy of the redemption notice by first class mail not less 
than 30 days prior to the date fixed for redemption to the holder of each Series 2022 Bond or portion of Series 2022 
Bond which is to be redeemed, at the address shown on the registration books of the City to be kept at the principal 
office of the Trustee; provided, however, that failure to give such notice by mail, or any defect therein, shall not 
affect the validity of the proceedings for the redemption of any other Series 2022 Bond. 
Book-Entry-Only System 
The Depository Trust Company, New York, New York ("DTC") will initially act as securities depository 
for the Series 2022 Bonds.  The Series 2022 Bonds will be issued as fully registered securities in the name of Cede 
& Co. (DTC's partnership nominee).  Upon issuance of the Series 2022 Bonds, one fully registered Series 2022 
Bond will be issued for each maturity of the Series 2022 Bonds as set forth on the cover page hereof, each in the 
aggregate principal amount of such maturity and will be deposited with DTC.  So long as Cede & Co., as nominee 
of DTC, is the registered owner of the Series 2022 Bonds, references herein to the holders or registered owners of 
the Series 2022 Bonds shall mean Cede & Co. and shall not mean the Beneficial Owners (hereinafter defined) of the 
Series 2022 Bonds. 3 
The information under this caption concerning DTC and DTC's book-entry system has been obtained from 
sources believed to be reliable, but the City does not take any responsibility for the accuracy or completeness 
thereof. 
DTC, the world's largest depository, is a limited-purpose trust company organized under the New York 
Banking Law, a "banking organization" within the meaning of the New York Banking Law, a member of the 
Federal Reserve System, a "clearing corporation" within the meaning of the New York Uniform Commercial Code, 
and a "clearing agency" registered pursuant to the provisions of Section 17A of the Securities Exchange Act of 
1934.  DTC holds and provides asset servicing for over 2.2 million issues of U.S. and non-U.S. equity, corporate and 
municipal debt issues, and money market instruments from over 100 countries that DTC's participants ("Direct 
Participants") deposit with DTC.  DTC also facilitates the post-trade settlement among Direct Participants of sales 
and other securities transactions in deposited securities through electronic computerized book-entry transfers and 
pledges between Direct Participants' accounts.  This eliminates the need for physical movement of securities 
certificates.  Direct Participants include both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers and dealers, banks, trust 
companies, clearing corporations and certain other organizations.  DTC is a wholly-owned subsidiary of The 
Depository Trust & Clearing Corporation ("DTCC").  DTCC, in turn, is owned by a number of Direct Participants of 
DTC and Members of the National Securities Clearing Corporation, Fixed Income Clearing Corporation and 
Emerging Markets Clearing Corporation (NSCC, FICC and EMCC, also subsidiaries of DTCC), as well as by the 
New York Stock Exchange, Inc., the American Stock Exchange LLC, and the National Association of Securities 
Dealers, Inc.  Access to the DTC system is also available to others such as both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers 
and dealers, banks, trust companies, and clearing corporations that clear through or maintain a custodial relationship 
with a Direct Participant, either directly or indirectly ("Indirect Participants").  DTC has a Standard & Poor's rating 
of AA+.  The DTC rules applicable to its Participants are on file with the Securities and Exchange Commission.  
More information about DTC can be found at www.dtcc.com. 
Purchases of Series 2022 Bonds under the DTC system must be made by or through Direct Participants, 
which will receive a credit for the Series 2022 Bonds on DTC's records.  The ownership interest of each actual 
purchaser of each Series 2022 Bond ("Beneficial Owner") is in turn to be recorded on the DTC Participants' records.  
Beneficial Owners will not receive written confirmation from DTC of their purchase.  Beneficial Owners are, 
however, expected to receive written confirmations providing details of the transaction, as well as periodic 
statements of their holdings, from the Direct or Indirect Participant through which the Beneficial Owner entered into 
the transaction.  Transfers of ownership interests in the Series 2022 Bonds are to be accomplished by entries made 
on the books of Direct and Indirect Participants acting on behalf of Beneficial Owners.  Beneficial Owners will not 
receive certificates representing their ownership interests in Series 2022 Bonds, except in the event that use of the 
book-entry system for the Series 2022 Bonds is discontinued. 
To facilitate subsequent transfers, all Series 2022 Bonds deposited by Direct Participants with DTC are 
registered in the name of DTC's partnership nominee, Cede & Co. or such other names may be requested by an 
authorized representative of DTC.  The deposit of Series 2022 Bonds with DTC and their registration in the name of 
Cede & Co. or such other nominee do not effect any change in beneficial ownership.  DTC has no knowledge of the 
actual Beneficial Owners of the Series 2022 Bonds; DTC's records reflect only the identity of the Direct Participants 
to whose accounts such Series 2022 Bonds are credited, which may or may not be the Beneficial Owners.  The 
Direct and Indirect Participants will remain responsible for keeping account of their holdings on behalf of their 
customers. 
The City and the Registrar/Paying Agent will recognize DTC or its nominee, Cede & Co., as the registered 
owner of the Series 2022 Bonds for all purposes.  Conveyance of notices and other communications by DTC to 
Direct Participants, by Direct Participants to Indirect Participants, and by Direct Participants and Indirect 
Participants to Beneficial Owners will be governed by arrangements among them, subject to any statutory or 
regulatory requirements as may be in effect from time to time. 
Redemption notices shall be sent to DTC.  If less than all of the Series 2022 Bonds are being redeemed, 
DTC's practice is to determine by lot the amount of the interest of each Direct Participant in such issue to be 
redeemed. 4 
Neither DTC nor Cede & Co. (nor such other DTC nominee) will consent or vote with respect to the Series 
2022 Bonds unless authorized by a Direct Participant in accordance with DTC's Procedures.  Under its usual 
procedures, DTC mails an Omnibus Proxy to the City as soon as possible after the record date.  The Omnibus Proxy 
assigns Cede & Co.'s consenting or voting rights to those Direct Participants to whose accounts the Series 2022 
Bonds are credited on the record date (identified on a listing attached to the Omnibus Proxy). 
Principal and interest payments on the Series 2022 Bonds will be made to Cede & Co., or such other 
nominee as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC.  DTC's practice is to credit DTC Participants' 
accounts, upon DTC's receipt of funds and corresponding detail information from the City or the Registrar/Paying 
Agent on the payable date in accordance with their respective holdings shown on DTC's records.  Payments by 
Participants to Beneficial Owners will be governed by standing instructions and customary practices, as is the case 
with securities held for the accounts of customers in bearer form or registered in "street name," and will be the 
responsibility of such Participant and not of DTC nor its nominee, the City or the Registrar/Paying Agent, subject to 
any statutory or regulatory requirements as may be in effect from time to time.  Payment of principal and interest to 
Cede & Co. (or such other nominee as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC) is the 
responsibility of the City acting through the Registrar/Paying Agent, disbursement of such payments to Direct 
Participants shall be the responsibility of DTC, and disbursement of such payments to the Beneficial Owners shall 
be the responsibility of Direct and Indirect Participants. 
Procedure in the Event of Discontinuation of Book-Entry Only System 
DTC may discontinue providing its services as securities depository with respect to the Series 2022 Bonds 
at any time by giving reasonable notice to the City or the Registrar/Paying Agent.  Under such circumstances, in the 
event that a successor securities depository is not obtained, Bond certificates are required to be printed and 
delivered. 
The City may decide to discontinue use of the system of book-entry-only transfers through DTC (or a 
successor securities depository).  In that event, Bond certificates will be printed and delivered to DTC. 
The Series 2022 Bonds will be issued in fully-registered form in the denominations of $5,000 or any whole 
multiple thereof, not exceeding the principal amount of the Series 2022 Bonds maturing in each year.  All Series 
2022 Bonds will be registered upon the registration books of the City which are to be kept for this purpose at the 
office of the Registrar and Paying Agent. 
Registration and Transfer 
Upon the discontinuance of the book-entry system, Series 2022 Bonds shall be evidenced by bond 
certificates issued in the name of the registered owners thereof as set forth on the registration books, and Series 2022 
Bonds shall be transferable only upon the registration books by the registered owner thereof in person or by his 
attorney duly authorized in writing, upon surrender thereof together with a written instrument of transfer satisfactory 
to the Trustee, duly executed by the registered owner or his duly authorized attorney.  Upon the transfer of any 
Series 2022 Bond, the City shall execute and thereupon the Trustee shall authenticate and deliver to the transferee a 
new fully registered Series 2022 Bond or Bonds, registered in the name of the transferee of the same aggregate 
principal amount, maturity and interest rate as the surrendered Series 2022 Bond. 
The City and the Trustee may deem and treat the person in whose name any Series 2022 Bond is registered 
as the absolute owner of such Series 2022 Bond for the purpose of receiving payment of the principal of, and interest 
on, such Series 2022 Bond and for all other purposes. 
For every exchange or transfer of any Series 2022 Bond, whether temporary or definitive, the City and the 
Trustee may make a charge sufficient to reimburse them for any tax, fee or other governmental charge required to be 
paid with respect to such exchange or transfer. 5 
SECURITY FOR THE SERIES 2022 BONDS 
Pledged Revenues; Special Obligations 
The Bond Ordinance provides that all bonds issued pursuant to such ordinance, including the Series 2022 
Bonds, shall be secured by a pledge of, and a lien upon, Gross Revenues (as such term is defined herein in Appendix 
C - "SUMMARY OF THE BOND ORDINANCE") less amounts required to fund the operation and maintenance of 
the City's waterworks and sewer system (the "System").  Such pledge securing the Bonds (as defined herein) shall at 
all times and in all respects remain superior to pledges made to secure other bonds or obligations payable out of the 
revenues of the System.

THE SERIES 2022 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE AN INDEBTEDNESS OF THE CITY 
WITHIN THE MEANING OF ANY PROVISION, LIMITATION OR RESTRICTION OF THE 
CONSTITUTION OR THE LAWS OF THE STATE OF SOUTH CAROLINA, OTHER THAN THOSE 
PROVISIONS AUTHORIZING INDEBTEDNESS PAYABLE SOLELY FROM A REVENUE-
PRODUCING PROJECT NOT INVOLVING REVENUES FROM ANY TAX OR LICENSE.  THE CITY IS 
NOT OBLIGATED TO PAY ANY OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS OR THE INTEREST THEREON 
EXCEPT FROM THE PLEDGED REVENUES DESCRIBED ABOVE. 
Debt Service Reserve Fund 
The Bond Ordinance provides that each Series Ordinance may provide for the establishment of a Debt 
Service Reserve Fund for each Series of Bonds. 
There will be no Reserve Requirement or Debt Service Reserve Fund for the Series 2022 Bonds. 
Other Accounts 
The Bond Ordinance establishes the General Revenue Fund, the Operation and Maintenance Fund, the 
Debt Service Fund and the Depreciation and Contingent Fund.  With certain limited exceptions, all Gross Revenues 
of the System shall be deposited in the General Revenue Fund.  So long as the City establishes proper records of 
receipts and disbursements, the General Revenue Fund may be used for the purposes of the Operation and 
Maintenance Fund. 6 
The Operation and Maintenance Fund is intended to provide for the payment of all expenses incurred in 
connection with the administration and operation of the System, including such expenses as may be reasonably 
necessary to preserve the System in good repair and working order.  Withdrawals from this fund shall be made by 
order of the Commissioners in accordance, as nearly as may be practicable, with the annual budget established by 
the Commissioners prior to the commencement of each fiscal year. 
The Debt Service Fund is intended to provide for the payment of the principal of, premium, if any, and 
interest on all Bonds as the same respectively fall due.  There shall be deposited into this fund the monthly fraction 
of the aggregate amount of interest to become due on the Bonds on the succeeding interest payment date and one 
twelfth of the aggregate amount of the principal of all Bonds becoming due and payable during the succeeding 
twelve months. 
The Depreciation and Contingent Fund is intended to provide a reasonable reserve for depreciation of the 
System, for contingencies and for improvements, betterment and extensions of the System.  The fund shall be 
maintained in an amount established at least annually by the Commissioners on the advice of the Commissioners' 
consulting engineers and may also be used to prevent defaults in payments to be made with respect to Bonds and to 
redeem Bonds.  As of December 31, 2021, $19,672,510 was on deposit in this fund. 
For a more detailed description of these funds, see in Appendix C - "SUMMARY OF THE BOND 
ORDINANCE -- Establishment of Funds". 
Rate Covenant 
The City has covenanted to maintain rates and charges for all services furnished by the System which at all 
times shall be sufficient: (i) to provide for the payment of the expenses of administration and operation and such 
expenses for maintenance of the System as may be necessary to preserve the same in good repair and working order; 
(ii) to provide for the punctual payment of the principal of and interest on all Bonds and all Junior Lien Bonds (as 
such term is defined in Appendix C - "SUMMARY OF THE BOND ORDINANCE") that may from time to time 
hereafter be outstanding; (iii) to maintain the Debt Service Fund in the manner described in the Bond Ordinance; 
(iv) to maintain any Debt Service Reserve Fund in the manner and at the levels required by the Bond Ordinance and 
any applicable Series Ordinance; (v) to build and maintain a reserve for depreciation of the System, for 
contingencies and for improvements, betterment and extensions of the System other than those necessary to 
maintain the same in good repair and working order; and (vi) to discharge all obligations imposed by the Act and the 
Bond Ordinance. 
The City has further covenanted to prescribe and maintain and thereafter collect rates and charges which, 
together with other income, are reasonably expected to yield annual Net Earnings (as such term is defined in 
Appendix C - "SUMMARY OF THE BOND ORDINANCE") in each year equal to at least 120% of the Annual 
Principal and Interest Requirement. 
The Bond Ordinance requires the City to revise such rates and charges as necessary in order that they shall 
at all times be maintained on a sufficient basis to comply with the foregoing requirements. 
Additional Bonds 
The City may issue from time to time additional obligations ("Additional Bonds") on a parity with the 
Bonds, subject to certain restrictive covenants set forth in the Bond Ordinance, which include: 
(i) on the occasion of the issuance of any Additional Bonds, there shall exist no default in 
the payment of the principal of or interest on any Bond or Junior Lien Bond then Outstanding; 
(ii) all Debt Service Reserve Funds, if any, shall be funded to the prescribed levels provided 
for in the Bond Ordinance or any applicable Series Ordinance with respect to all Bonds to be Outstanding 
immediately following the issuance of such Additional Bonds; 7 
(iii) except in the case of Bonds issued for the purpose of refunding any Bonds: (A) Net 
Earnings during the fiscal year immediately preceding the fiscal year in which such Series of Bonds is to be 
issued, adjusted to reflect any rate increases currently adopted and to be in effect prior to or coincident with 
the date of issuance of such Bonds, and determined pro forma as though such rate increases had been in 
continuous effect during such preceding fiscal year, shall be not less than 120% of the Annual Principal and 
Interest Requirement of the current fiscal year for all Bonds Outstanding immediately prior to the proposed 
issuance; and (B) for each of the five fiscal years following the later of the date of the delivery of the Bonds 
of such series, or the period, if any, for which interest is funded from the proceeds of such Bonds, Net 
Earnings, as shall have been forecasted by an authorized officer of the Commissioners, shall be not less 
than 120% of the Annual Principal and Interest Requirement on all Bonds then proposed to be Outstanding 
in each of such five fiscal years; and 
(iv) in the case of Bonds issued for the purpose of refunding any Bonds either: (A) the Annual 
Principal and Interest Requirement of the refunding Bonds shall not exceed the Annual Principal and 
Interest Requirement of the refunded Bonds until a time subsequent to the last maturity of Bonds not 
refunded and which remain Outstanding following the issuance of the refunding Bonds; or (B) the City 
shall comply with the earnings tests described in (A) and (B) of paragraph (iii) above.

2022 Construction Fund 
A portion of the proceeds of the offering of the Series 2022 Bonds in the approximate amount of 
$161,398,346 will be deposited into a construction fund (the "2022 Construction Fund") established pursuant to the 
Resolution.  Money on deposit in the 2022 Construction Fund, plus earnings thereon, will be used, as needed, to 
finance the costs of the Projects, including without limitation payment of engineering, legal and all other expenses 
incidental to the Projects.  Until such time as money on deposit in the 2022 Construction Fund is applied to the costs 
of the Projects, such money shall be invested and reinvested in Authorized Investments (as such term is defined 
herein in Appendix C - "SUMMARY OF THE BOND ORDINANCE").  All earnings therefrom shall be added to 
and become a part of the 2022 Construction Fund.  The 2022 Construction Fund shall be held, maintained and 
controlled by the Commissioners.   8 
THE PROJECTS 
The Projects to be financed with a portion of the proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds consist of new and 
replacement infrastructure in the water distribution system and the wastewater collection system and improvements 
at the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant and the Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant.  Comprehensive 20-year 
master plans were prepared by engineering consultants in conjunction with System engineers for the water 
distribution system, the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant, the wastewater collection system and the Plum Island 
Wastewater Treatment Plant.  Portions of the master plans will be implemented as part of the 2022-2027 Capital 
Improvements Program (see "THE CAPITAL IMPROVEMENTS PROGRAM" herein) and will be funded with 
proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds and System revenues as described below. 
The master plan for the water distribution system addresses both rehabilitation or replacement of the 
existing distribution system infrastructure and improvements to meet projected water demands associated with 
future growth.  Extensive hydraulic computer modeling of the water distribution system was performed to identify 
infrastructure needs and to develop a phased construction program.  Proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds will be used 
to finance water distribution system improvements including a 30-inch transmission main, a 24-inch transmission 
main, rehabilitation and replacement of deteriorated water mains, and relocation of numerous water mains to 
accommodate roadway and drainage improvements projects. 
The master plan for the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant addresses adequacy of existing water supply and 
treatment facilities to meet projected future demands associated with growth and proposed treatment goals of 
anticipated water quality regulations.  The master plan evaluates process alternatives and incorporates recommended 
improvements into a phased construction program.  Proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds will be used to finance 
improvements at the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant including numerous projects that will expand the hydraulic 
capacity from 115.4 MGD to 127.4 MGD to meet projected peak day water demands. 
The master plan for the wastewater collection system addresses both rehabilitation or replacement of the 
existing collection system infrastructure and improvements to meet projected wastewater flows associated with 
future growth. Extensive hydraulic modeling of the wastewater collection system was performed to identify 
infrastructure needs and to develop a phased construction program.  Proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds will be used 
to finance wastewater collection system improvements including extension of the West Ashely Sewer Tunnel, pump 
station and collection system rehabilitation, and relocation of numerous sewer mains to accommodate roadway and 
drainage improvements projects. 
The master plan for the Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant addresses adequacy of existing treatment 
facilities to meet projected future flows associated with growth and proposed treatment goals of anticipated 
discharge regulations.  The master plan evaluates process alternatives and incorporates recommended improvements 
into a phased construction program.  Proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds will be used to finance improvements at the 
Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant including replacement of deteriorated biosolids thickening and dewatering 
facilities and the addition of a biosolids thermal dryer facility to reduce or eliminate the risk of rapidly changing 
requirements and increasing fees for biosolids disposal at landfills. 
The Commissioners also plan to renovate its headquarters building to ensure the ability of the 
Commissioners to continue to serve its customers at its St. Philip Street location in peninsula Charleston for the 
foreseeable future. 9

THE WATERWORKS AND SEWER SYSTEM 
Description of the System 
The Waterworks Utility
The City of Charleston originally received its public water supply from artesian wells which, after the 
installation of air-lift pumps, provided 2 million gallons per day ("MGD") to the residents of the City.  By the year 
1897, however, this yield was inadequate to meet the demands of the City.  Thus, the Charleston Light and Water 
Company constructed a dam across the marshlands of Goose Creek, a tidal tributary of the Cooper River, at a point 
approximately 12 miles from the City.  The Goose Creek System then consisted of a fresh water reservoir with a 
capacity yield of 5 MGD, a sedimentation basin, a treatment plant, steam pumps, a wood stave distribution line 
made of tongue-and-groove California Redwood, and 11 miles of 24-inch cast iron supply mains. 10 
In 1917, the City purchased the assets and properties of the Charleston Light and Water Company, and the 
Commissioners of Public Works was established by legislative act to manage and direct the activities of the System.  
At that time, there were approximately 7,000 taps on the System, which had a total value of $1,360,000.  In 1921, 
the City acquired additional waterworks properties from Goose Creek Land Company.  In 1984, the Commissioners 
acquired these properties and other assets that are part of the System from the City. 
The area currently served by the waterworks utility, more fully described herein under the heading "THE 
SERVICE AREA AND ITS ECONOMY," includes nearly all of the developed metropolitan area lying inside and 
outside the City limits between the Stono and Wando Rivers.  This area includes the municipalities of Charleston, 
North Charleston, Hanahan, James Island, Folly Beach, Sullivan's Island, Goose Creek, Lincolnville, Hollywood, 
Meggett and Ravenel, as well as the unincorporated areas of West Ashley, James Island, Johns Island, the Cainhoy 
Peninsula and the southern portions of Berkeley and Dorchester Counties as well as Joint Base Charleston, and a 
portion of the water used by the Town of Mt. Pleasant and the City of Isle of Palms.  The Towns of Kiawah Island 
and Seabrook Island are served indirectly through wholesale water sales to St. Johns Water Company which is the 
System's largest wholesale customer.   
The System provided water service to an average of 124,097 accounts in 2021, including approximately 
53,719 located within the corporate limits of the City.  The System is entirely metered except for approximately 
2,072 unmetered fire service accounts. 
The entire service area is supplied with treated water from the 115.4 MGD-capacity Hanahan Water 
Treatment Plant located approximately 12 miles north of the City.  The Hanahan Plant, which the Commissioners 
acquired from the City in 1984, consists of raw water pumps, sedimentation basins, filter units, high-service pumps 
together with stand-by diesel pumps on both the low and high-service pumping stations and clearwell basins for 
storage.  In addition to the 12,500,000 gallons of clearwell capacity with associated high-service pumps located at 
the treatment plant, five ground-level storage tanks and one elevated storage tank, with a combined capacity of 
21,500,000 gallons, help to maintain uniform service pressure throughout the System and meet peak System 
demands.  The distribution from the Hanahan Plant is through two 48-inch mains, one 36-inch main, one 30-inch 
main, three 24-inch mains, one 20-inch main and one 16-inch main.  These mains are inter-connected in several 
places so that a shutdown of one main will not seriously interrupt service in the distribution system.  The System's 
treated water transmission and distribution system includes over 1,838 miles of water mains varying in size with a 
maximum diameter of 48 inches. 
One of the two primary sources of water for the Hanahan Plant is the Edisto River.  Raw water is obtained 
from the river and conveyed to the plant by an unlined tunnel through Cooper marl. 1  The Kinard Tunnel, which was 
completed in 1937, is seven feet in diameter and 23.5 miles long.  The present capacity of the Kinard Tunnel and 
Intake is 100 MGD, of which approximately 50 MGD is contractually obligated until November 20, 2046 to 
WestRock Company.  The second primary source of water is the Bushy Park Reservoir, which is connected to the 
Hanahan Plant by the McDowell Tunnel, an underground, unlined tunnel eight feet in diameter and approximately 
seven miles long, which has a capacity of 150 MGD.  The Commissioners enjoy statutory control of the Bushy Park 
Reservoir, the major surface water source for the greater Charleston area.  Well water in the area is limited. 
The St. Johns Water Company (which provides water to the unincorporated portions of Johns Island and to 
the municipalities of Kiawah Island and Seabrook Island), Dorchester County, Mt. Pleasant Waterworks ("MPW"), 
Berkeley County Water and Sanitation Authority ("BCWS") and Joint Base Charleston are currently the five largest 
treated water customers, accounting for approximately 8.39%, 3.09%, 2.48%, 1.65% and 1.45%, respectively, of 
2021 waterworks revenues and approximately 4.36%, 1.61%, 1.29%, 0.86% and 0.75%, respectively, of total 
operating revenues of the System.  See "Waterworks Utility – Largest Water Users – 2021" herein. 
In 2021, the Commissioners' largest water customer was the St. Johns Water Company.  The St. Johns 
Water Company was organized in 1976 and joined with the areas of Kiawah Island ("Kiawah") and Seabrook Island 
("Seabrook") to secure a water system to serve the area.  Established as a cooperatively owned and operated 
1The geology of the Charleston area includes a limestone formation known as "marl", which lies approximately 40 
feet below the surface of the earth.  When exposed to air, the marl in the Charleston area hardens, resulting in a 
suitable water tunnel that does not require any additional pipe or lining. 11 
company, the St. Johns Water Company is governed by a Board of Directors which is elected by its members.  
Agreements and contracts between the parties were signed in 1978 allocating a quantity of water to each entity 
based upon a 6.0 MGD water supply agreement with the Commissioners.  The original system obtained water from 
the Limehouse crossing of the Stono River at which point it was metered into the St. Johns System.  In 1991, a 
second connection to the system was installed on Maybank Highway and metered.  To keep up with increasing 
demands, a third master metered supply main from the Commissioners was completed in 2008 near Riverbend 
Drive.  The agreement between St. Johns Water Company and the Commissioners was amended to increase the 
water supply to 12.0 MGD, increasing to 14.5 MGD in 2015.  The contract was extended in 2007 for 40 years to 
2047. 
In 1979, the Commissioners entered into a contract, renewable on an annual basis, to provide potable water 
to the five Department of Defense installations in the Charleston area (Charleston Naval Base, Charleston Air Force 
Base, Naval Hospital, Naval Weapons Station and Naval Weapons Annex).  The Charleston Naval Base (and 
Shipyard) and the Naval Weapons Annex were closed on April 1, 1996.  Subsequent to the closure, the 
Commissioners assumed ownership of the waterworks distribution system servicing the former Naval Base and 
Shipyard.  The Naval Base has transitioned to private use under the Charleston Regional Development Authority.  In 
January 2010, the three remaining Department of Defense installations became Joint Base Charleston, one of ten 
joint bases operating under the Department of Defense.  The Naval Hospital ceased operation in 2012.  In 2013, the 
Commissioners entered into a 10-year contract to provide water service which superseded prior contracts.  The 
Commissioners are currently negotiating an extension of the contract. 
The Commissioners have entered into long-term contracts to provide raw water to certain companies 
including WestRock Company, located in the City of North Charleston, and INEOS US Chemical Company 
(formerly B.P. Cooper River), DAK Americas LLC and Cooper River Partners, LLC, located in or near the Bushy 
Park Industrial Complex in Berkeley County.  Two of the raw water contracts were extended in 2017.  In October 
2017, KapStone Paper and Packaging Corporation signed a 30-year revised contract extension, and in November 
2017, Cooper River Partners, LLC signed a 50-year revised contract extension.  In November 2018, Kapstone Paper 
and Package Corporation was acquired by WestRock Company.  The aggregate revenues derived from these 
contracts accounted for 0.42% of 2021 operating revenues of the waterworks utility. 
The Commissioners have entered into long-term contracts with St. Johns Water Company, BCWS, the City 
of Folly Beach, the Town of Lincolnville and Dorchester County to provide each with wholesale potable water 
service.  The Commissioners have also entered into 30-year retail service area agreements with the City of Hanahan 
and the Town of Hollywood, a 15-year retail service area agreement with the Town of Ravenel, and a 20-year retail 
service area extension agreement with the City of Goose Creek which runs until 2034.  The Commissioners' two 
retail service area contracts with BCWS run through October 27, 2022 and October 31, 2023.  The Commissioners 
are currently negotiating 30-year extensions of both contracts. 
The Commissioners provide wholesale potable water to the Isle of Palms Waterworks and Sewer 
Commission ("IOPWSC") and the MPW under separate purchased capacity contractual agreements.  The supply of 
water to IOPWSC began in April 1997, and the MPW service was activated in September 1997.  The current 
contract capacity for IOPWSC and MPW is 1.50 MGD and 6.00 MGD, respectively.  Revenues received from the 
IOPWSC and MPW for water in 2021 totaled $368,234 and $2,039,246, respectively.  In addition to the volumetric 
revenues, these purchased capacity customers are charged a proportional share of the capital assets used to treat and 
supply water.  These annual payments to the Commissioners are not considered revenue but are treated as 
contributed capital and are assessed based on a percentage of total treatment capacity of the Hanahan Water 
Treatment Plant which is applied yearly to completed projects related to the treatment and transmission of water for 
IOPWSC and MPW.  The amounts of contributed capital billed to IOPWSC and MPW for fiscal year 2021 are 
$10,867 and $33,657, respectively.  All of these funds are used to offset future capital improvements.  
The Commissioners also provide wholesale water to the Town of Sullivan's Island under a purchased 
capacity contractual agreement similar to those between the Commissioners and IOPWSC and MPW described in 
the immediately preceding paragraph.  Service to the Town of Sullivan's Island was activated in 1996.  The current 
contract capacity for the Town of Sullivan's Island is 0.75 MGD.  The amount that is required to be paid by the 
Town of Sullivan's Island pursuant to its contract with the Commissioners is currently in dispute.  The Town of 
Sullivan's Island is currently paying an amount based on its interpretation of the contract rate formula, to which the 12 
Commissioners object. As a result, the Town of Sullivan's Island is only paying a portion of the amount being billed 
by the Commissioners.  Water charges billed to the Town of Sullivan's Island in 2021 totaled $173,036, and the 
amount paid totaled $121,598.  The amount of contributed capital billed to the Town of Sullivan's Island for 2021 is 
$5,476.  As of December 31, 2021, the Town of Sullivan's Island owed the Commissioners a cumulative total of 
$668,092 based on the Commissioners' interpretation of the contract for both volumetric and capital charges for the 
years 2016 through 2021.  The Commissioners notified the Town of Sullivan's Island on August 5, 2019 that the 
contract will terminate at the end of its current term on July 19, 2024.  
The Commissioners provide retail water service to an average of 51,444 accounts within the City of North 
Charleston ("North Charleston"), and much of the adjacent areas surrounding North Charleston.  The 
Commissioners have provided retail water service to the residents of North Charleston both prior to and since North 
Charleston was incorporated in 1972.  On December 9, 2004, North Charleston and the Commissioners executed a 
Retail Water Supply and Service Area Agreement granting the Commissioners the right to continue to provide retail 
water service to North Charleston for 30 years.  Presently, these customers use approximately 16.11 MGD of 
potable water, which accounted for approximately 44.6% of 2021 waterworks revenues and approximately 23.2% of 
total operating revenue.  
In 1991, the City of Charleston annexed Daniel Island, which consists of 4,500 acres, and a portion of the 
Cainhoy Peninsula, consisting of 5,300 acres, bringing these areas into the Commissioners' service area.  As of 
December 31, 2021, the Commissioners provided water and wastewater service to an average of 7,166 customers on 
Daniel Island and the Cainhoy Peninsula.  Total water consumption billed in 2021 was 1,070,299 Ccf, with 2021 
water and wastewater sales totaling $3,565,061 and $6,968,171, respectively. 13

The Wastewater Utility 
The wastewater utility provided service to an average of 59,781 retail accounts in 2021, including service 
to an average of 52,266 wastewater accounts inside the corporate limits of the City and 7,515 outside of the 
corporate limits of the City including unincorporated areas of Johns Island, Cainhoy and West Ashley.  The 
Commissioners also serve four wholesale accounts with the Towns of Meggett, Hollywood and Ravenel and James 
Island Public Service District which, as of their fiscal year ended June 30, 2021, provides service to approximately 
7,174 direct service connections within the James Island Public Service District and approximately 1,575 indirect 
service connections in the City of Folly Beach which flow through the James Island Public Service District system.  
Medical University of South Carolina, James Island Public Service District, City of Charleston Housing Authority, 17 
Roper Hospital and Charleston County School District are the five largest customers, accounting for approximately 
3.95%, 3.88%, 2.29%, 1.07% and 1.04%, respectively, of 2021 wastewater revenues and approximately 1.68%, 
1.65%, 0.98%, 0.46% and 0.44%, respectively, of the 2021 total operating revenues of the System.  See 
"Wastewater Utility – Largest Wastewater Users – 2021". 
The Commissioners assumed responsibility for operating and maintaining the sewage disposal system of 
the City when the waterworks utility and the wastewater utility were combined into the Waterworks and Sewer 
System of the City of Charleston in 1961.  The original wastewater utility, built in 1895, consisted of collector lines 
and small pumping stations.  Since assuming responsibility for operating and maintaining the wastewater system at 
the beginning of 1961, the Commissioners have acted to meet state and federal environmental control regulations by 
constructing a sanitary sewer system to collect and convey all the wastewater flow of the West Ashley, James 
Island, Daniel Island, Cainhoy and Peninsula areas of the City to the 36-MGD Plum Island Wastewater Treatment 
Plant which the Commissioners acquired from the City in 1981.  The sanitary sewer system comprises 
approximately 628 miles of conventional gravity sewers, 129.8 miles of force mains, and approximately 12 miles of 
deep level interceptor tunnels.  The wastewater conveyed by the sanitary sewer system is given primary and 
secondary treatment at the Plum Island Treatment Plant.  The secondary facilities at this plant were placed in 
operation in 1984.  In 1997, the Commissioners received an up-rating of the Plum Island Wastewater Treatment 
Plant capacity from 27 MGD to 36 MGD.  This upgrade was accomplished through a detailed in-house engineering 
evaluation which included a computer simulation model and historical treatment performance at superior levels.  For 
outstanding past performance, the Commissioners were awarded the National Association of Clean Water Agencies 
("NACWA") award for large treatment plants achieving advanced levels of treatment.  (See "Awards and 
Recognitions" herein).  Treated wastewater from the treatment plant is released through an outfall sewer extending 
approximately 4,000 feet into Charleston Harbor.   
In 1995, the Commissioners acquired approximately 22 acres of land on Daniel Island from the Daniel 
Island Development Company, Inc. as the site for a proposed wastewater treatment plant.  During the following 
year, the Commissioners placed into operation the Daniel Island Wastewater Treatment Plant.  Initially constructed 
for 0.250 MGD, the plant capacity was expanded to 0.500 MGD in 2001 and then to 0.9 MGD in 2006 to keep up 
with increasing demands.  Because of the stringent discharge permit ("NPDES") issued in 2005 by the South 
Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control ("DHEC"), the Commissioners determined that it was 
not feasible to re-rate the plant capacity for more than 4.0 MGD.  Accordingly, the Commissioners determined that 
the most cost-effective treatment option was to divert the wastewater flow from Daniel Island and Cainhoy to the 
Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant.  The Daniel Island Tunnel Project, which accomplished this diversion of 
flow in 2008, was part of the 2006-2009 Capital Improvements Program.  The discharge permit for the Daniel Island 
Wastewater Treatment Plant remains in effect for use if needed although the plant does not discharge at this time. 
In 2010, after a lengthy field study and development of a three-dimensional water quality model, the 
Berkeley-Charleston-Dorchester Council of Governments ("BCD COG") issued a final Total Maximum Daily Load 
("TMDL") for the Ashley and Cooper Rivers and Charleston Harbor.  The TMDL allows the Daniel Island 
Wastewater Treatment Plant 4.0 MGD of flow and 403 pounds of Ultimate Oxygen Demand ("UOD") capacity.  
The Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant is allowed 54 MGD of flow and 24,612 pounds of UOD in the final 
BCD COG recommendation.  The TMDL has been approved by both the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency 
("EPA") and DHEC.   
NPDES permits for both the Plum Island and the Daniel Island Wastewater Treatment Plants run through 
July 31, 2024.  The Plum Island Plant reported four daily maximum bacteria violations of its NPDES permit in 
November 2018 and March 2019 due to dewatering equipment issues and resultant excessive solids inventory.  
DHEC placed the Plum Island Plant under a Consent Order in April 2019, which the Commissioners addressed 
through a corrective action plan completed in October 2019.  DHEC closed the Consent Order in March 2020.  
There have been no further permit excursions to date. 18

Operations of the System 
The System is governed by the Commissioners, comprised of three Commissioners elected at large by the 
voters of the City to six-year staggered terms, and the Mayor of the City and a member of the City Council who 
serve as ex-officio members.  Except for borrowing money through the issuance of bonds or bond anticipation notes, 
the Commissioners have complete charge of the System.  In such instances in which bonds or notes must be issued 
or the rights of bondholders or noteholders must be protected, the City Council is granted jurisdiction.  In the course 
of a contest between the City Council of Spartanburg, South Carolina and the Commissioners of Public Works of the 
City of Spartanburg, South Carolina, whose powers are identical to those of the Commissioners, the Supreme Court 
of South Carolina declared: 
It is our conclusion that the power to fix rates, dispose of surplus revenue, and otherwise control 
and direct the fiscal policies of the waterworks system of the City of Spartanburg is vested in the 
Commissioners of Public Works so long as that body fulfills the covenants and agreements for the 
protection of the bondholders set forth in the ordinance authorizing the issuance of revenue bonds, but if 
the Commissioners fail or neglect to carry out these covenants and obligations, the City Council may 
enforce compliance. 
In addition to operating the System, the Commissioners control certain properties (the "Property") acquired 
by the City when it purchased the assets of the Charleston Light and Water Company in 1917 as well as other 
property acquired from time to time thereafter.  From time to time the Commissioners have sold parcels from the 
Property.  The Property is listed as an asset of the Commissioners and is carried at book value on the balance sheet 
of the Commissioners. 
Regulation 
The Commissioners' rates and collection procedures are not subject to approval by any other administrative 
body.  Such rates and procedures are subject to judicial review upon action of a ratepayer.  The Commissioners 
believe their rates and collection procedures are reasonable under applicable legal standards.  The Commissioners 
have utilized the nationally recognized firm of Black & Veatch to perform all of its rate analysis work for over four 
decades.  There have been no successful rate challenges to the Commission-established rates in its history. 
Potable water quality and wastewater effluent quality are subject to regulation by the EPA and the South 
Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control. 22 
Awards and Recognitions 
In 1999, the Commissioners became the first public water or wastewater utility in the United States to 
become registered in conformance with the Environmental Management System standards of the International 
Organization for Standardization, ISO 14001.  Certification has been continually maintained through annual audits 
since that time.  In October 2018, the Commissioners were certified in accordance with 2015 revisions to the ISO 
14001 Standard.  In 2011, the Commissioners received the South Carolina Governor's Quality Award.  This award is 
based on the National Malcolm Baldrige Quality Award and recognizes organizations that demonstrate excellent 
performance through a quality management system.  In 2011 through 2019 and again in 2021, the Commissioners 
were included in the top 25 large company rankings of Best Places to Work in South Carolina as announced by the 
South Carolina Chamber of Commerce.   
The Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant has been recognized for perfect permit compliance by the 
National Association of Clean Water Agencies ("NACWA").  The Commissioners were awarded the Platinum 
Award by NACWA in 2014 for the Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant in recognition of seven consecutive 
years without a permit excursion.  The Plum Island Plant received a Silver Award in 2015 and the Gold Award in 
2016, 2017, 2018 and 2021 from NACWA. 
The Hanahan Water Treatment Plant entered into a voluntary Partnership for Safe Water agreement with 
the EPA in December 1995.  The primary purpose of the Partnership for Safe Water is to encourage U.S. water 
suppliers to assess their facilities, treatment processes, operating and maintenance procedures, and management 
oversight practices. On October 10, 2016, Hanahan Water Treatment Plant received the Presidents Award, 
representing optimized treatment to provide the safest water possible to CPW's customers.

The Chief Executive Officer of the System is responsible for the overall functioning of the System.  He 
reports to the Commissioners and carries out the policies set by the Commissioners.  Floyd K. (Kin) Hill, Jr., P.E. 
was appointed Chief Executive Officer in July 2006.  Mr. Hill has been employed by the Commissioners since 1987, 
serving as Director of Wastewater Operations, Director of Collection and Distribution and Chief Operating Officer 
prior to becoming C.E.O.  Before coming to CPW, he was Director of a District Office of the S.C. Department of 
Health and Environmental Control.  He is a member of the American Water Works Association, Water Environment 
Federation, and Automated Meter Reading Association.  Mr. Hill holds a Bachelor of Science Degree in 
Agricultural Engineering from Clemson University and a Master's Degree in Environmental and Water Resources 
Engineering from the University of South Carolina.  Mr. Hill is a Registered Professional Engineer in the State of 
South Carolina and an "A" Level licensed Water Distribution and Wastewater Collection System Operator.  Mr. Hill 
recently announced his retirement effective August 2022. 
The Assistant Chief Executive Officer is Mark Cline, P.E. who will succeed Mr. Hill as Chief Executive 
Officer of the System upon Mr. Hill's retirement in August 2022.  Mr. Cline is principally responsible for overseeing 
the Water Treatment Process, the Water Distribution System, the Wastewater Collection System, the Wastewater 
Treatment Facilities and the Laboratory, with managerial oversight of the Capital Improvements Program.  Mr. 
Cline has been employed by the Commissioners since 1984, serving as Engineering Manager, Superintendent and 23 
Plant Engineer for the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant, Senior Director of Design and Construction and Capital 
Projects Officer before becoming Assistant Chief Executive Officer in 2018.  Mr. Cline is a member of the 
American Water Works Association, the Water Environment Federation and the American Society of Civil 
Engineers.  He holds a Bachelor of Science Degree in Civil Engineering from North Carolina State University and is 
licensed as a Professional Engineer and a Water Treatment Plant Operator. 
The Chief Administrative Officer is Dorothy G. Harrison, who directs the operations of Compliance and 
Audit Services, Customer Service, Human Resources and Public Relations.  Ms. Harrison has been employed by the 
Commissioners since July 2001.  Prior to joining CPW, Ms. Harrison spent 26 years in the banking industry and was 
among the first African American commercial loan officers and vice presidents in the State of South Carolina.  Ms. 
Harrison was also one of the first bankers in South Carolina to serve a dual role in the industry as a licensed broker 
and commercial banker.  She is a member of the American Water Works Association and the Water Environment 
Federation and is an active member of numerous boards and foundations.  She attended the University of South 
Carolina and George Mason University, with studies in Business Administration and Psychology, and is a graduate 
of East Carolina School of Banking. 
The Chief Financial Officer is Wesley Ropp, CMA, CP 3P-F, who is responsible for the financial operations 
of the System, including the Accounting, Budgeting, Finance, Purchasing, Records Management and Information 
Technology functions.  Mr. Ropp joined CPW in 1982 as an accountant, later serving as Administrator of 
Accounting, Administrator of Finance and Senior Director of Financial Services.  Mr. Ropp is a Certified 
Management Accountant and a Certified PPP Professional - Foundation.  He holds a Bachelor of Science Degree in 
Business Administration with emphasis in Accounting from the College of Charleston and a Master's Degree in 
Business Administration from The Citadel. 
The Capital Projects Officer is Russell L. Huggins, Jr., P.E., who is responsible for overseeing the 
operations of Engineering and Construction, Asset Management and Geographic Information Systems, Safety and 
Support Services and the SCADA System.  Mr. Huggins joined CPW in January 1999 as an engineer in the Design 
and Construction Department. He became Engineering Manager in 2004, Director of Engineering in 2006, and 
Director of Engineering and Construction in 2015 before becoming Capital Projects Officer in 2018.  Mr. Huggins 
earned his Bachelors of Science Degree in Civil Engineering and Master's Degree in Business Administration from 
The Citadel.  He is licensed as a Professional Engineer and as a Wastewater Treatment Plant Operator and is a 
member of the American Water Works Association, the Water Environment Federation and the American Society of 
Civil Engineers. 
Employees 
All employees in established positions participate in the South Carolina State Retirement System as well as 
the Social Security System of the Federal Government.  All such employees are non-union. 
The Commissioners' 2021 budget authorized 458 positions.  As of December 31, 2021, the Commissioners 
had 416 of this authorized number of employees in the following positions: 
Officers and Managers 58 
Professionals and Technicians 106 
Clerical 76 
Operating and Maintenance 176 
Total 416 
Fringe Benefits, Retirement and Health Insurance 
All employees of the System participate in a defined benefit pension plan administered by the State of 
South Carolina, the South Carolina Retirement System ("SCRS"), which is a cost-sharing, multiple-employer public 
employee retirement plan.  The total payroll for employees covered by the SCRS for the year ended December 31, 
2021 was $27,458,419. The SCRS offers retirement and disability benefits, cost-of-living adjustments on an ad-hoc 
basis, life insurance benefits and survivor benefits.  The plans' provisions are established under Title 9 of the Code 
of Laws of South Carolina 1976, as amended ("Title 9"). 24 
Both employees and the System are required to contribute to the SCRS at rates established under the 
authority of Title 9.  The System's contributions are actuarially determined, but are communicated to and paid by the 
System as a percentage of the employee's annual earnings.  For the fiscal years ended December 31, 2021, 2020 and 
2019, the System contributed 100% of the required contributions.  Contributions by the System for employees 
covered by the SCRS amounted to $4,373,378 for the fiscal year ended December 31, 2021, $4,311,165 for the 
fiscal year ended December 31, 2020 and $3,934,695 for the fiscal year ended December 31, 2019.  Employee 
contributions for the SCRS were based on 9% of the employees' earnings and amounted to $2,471,258 for the fiscal 
year ended December 31, 2021, $2,493,605 for the fiscal year ended December 31, 2020 and $2,350,064 for the 
fiscal year ended December 31, 2019.  Legislation enacted by the State in 2017 increased the employer contribution 
rate to 13.56% beginning July 1, 2017 with five subsequent 1% increases through July 1, 2023, resulting in the 
employer contribution rate being capped at 18.56% and employee contribution rate capped at 9%. 
The System has paid all required contributions for fringe benefits and insurance as they have come due.  
There are no liabilities for underfunding of such benefits. 
GASB 75 – Accounting and Financial Reporting for Other Post Employment Benefits  
Government Accounting Standards Board Statement No. 75 ("GASB 75") establishes accounting and 
financial reporting requirements for state and local governments who have other post employment benefit ("OPEB") 
plans.  In order to comply with the requirements of GASB 75, the System contracted with Cavanaugh McDonald 
Consulting, LLC to perform an actuarial valuation to determine the Total OPEB Liability ("TOL"), the Net OPEB 
Liability ("NOL") and the Fiduciary Net Position ("FNP").  For the fiscal year ended December 31, 2021, the TOL 
is $60,138,427 with a FNP of $20,959,701, resulting in a NOL of $39,178,726.  The FNP is currently at 34.85% of 
TOL and is held in escrow with the South Carolina Other Retirement Benefits Trust ("SC ORBET"), a trust 
established for the purpose of sharing administrative and investment expenses in meeting GASB requirements. 
Rates and Charges of the System 
The Commissioners maintain rates of the System sufficient to meet the cash requirements of the System 
which include (i) System operation and maintenance expense, (ii) debt service requirements, including reserve fund 
payments, on bonded debt and (iii) expenditures for capital improvements not financed from Bond proceeds or 
contributions. 
Since 1975, the Commissioners have retained Black & Veatch Corporation (the "Consulting Engineers") to 
prepare analyses of the revenue requirements, costs of service and rate structures of the water and wastewater 
systems.  In preparing their studies, the Consulting Engineers review the projected requirements and consider the 
costs of maintaining and operating the System, required capital improvements and debt service payments.  Total 
costs of services are allocated equitably to the various classes of customers served by each utility, taking into 
consideration the nature and extent of the service provided to each class.  Based on studies conducted by the 
Consulting Engineers, the Commissioners adopted adjusted schedules of rates designed to achieve the following 
revenue increases shown in the table below.  The last rate increase became effective on January 1, 2022.

Existing rates and charges for water and wastewater services, which were implemented January 1, 2022, 
are structured to recognize the results of 2021 cost studies conducted by the Consulting Engineers and other 
practical considerations.  In connection with the approval of the 2022 annual budget, the Commissioners approved 
further rate increases of 5% for water and 6% for wastewater to become effective on January 1, 2023 and January 1, 
2024.  Reports presenting results of these studies formed the basis for the Consulting Engineers' recommendation.  
Comprehensive studies by the Consulting Engineers of multi-year revenue requirements, costs of service and rates, 
including consideration of capital project funding provided by the proceeds of bond issues, are performed 
periodically.  The last comprehensive study was done in 2021. 
Consistent with the requirements of the Bond Ordinance, it has been and continues to be the policy of the 
Commissioners periodically to review the rates and charges imposed upon its customers to ensure the generation of 
revenues sufficient to meet the cash requirements of the System described above (see Appendix C - "SUMMARY 
OF THE BOND ORDINANCE - Rate Covenant" and "-- Additional Covenants"). 
Revenues generated by the System are used in part to finance the cost of certain major water and 
wastewater capital improvements to the System as well as recurring annual capital improvements including 
replacements, extensions and minor improvements to the System's infrastructure.  The levels of expenditures for 
improvements financed from a combination of current and retained earnings, moneys transferred from the land

Water Tap and Impact Fees 
The Commissioners charge a water tap fee at the time of application for water service to recover the 
Commissioners' costs to install water service.  The Commissioners also charge water and wastewater impact fees to 
offset a portion of the costs of additional water and wastewater facilities necessary to meet the service requirements 
of new customers.  These impact fees are designed to reduce the magnitude and impact of future general rate 
increases, while attempting to allocate in a more equitable manner the costs associated with new development by 
imposing a service fee upon the developer at the commencement of new development activities. 
The water tap fee schedule shown below has been in effect since January 1, 1991, and the current water 
impact fees presented below became effective on July 1, 2018.  The Commissioners have approved increases to the 
impact fees which will become effective on July 1, 2022 and July 1, 2023.

Town of Hollywood 
Under the terms of a 2003 agreement with the Town of Hollywood, the Commissioners provide wholesale 
wastewater transportation and treatment services to the Hollywood/Petersfield area at a current rate of $3.19/Ccf 
applied to the Town's share of total flow through a master meter located near the point of discharge to the System.  
CPW also provides retail customer billing and collection services.  The Town is responsible for the operation and 
maintenance of its wastewater collection system. 
Town of Ravenel 
Under the terms of a 2006 agreement with the Town of Ravenel, the Commissioners provide wholesale 
wastewater transportation and treatment services to the Ravenel area at a current rate of $3.19/Ccf.  CPW also 
provides retail customer billing and collection services.  The Town of Ravenel is responsible for the operation and 30 
maintenance of its wastewater collection system.  The Town approved a rate and fee schedule in March 2008, 
finalized billing procedures in November 2008, and the first customer signed up for service in December 2008. 
Town of Meggett 
Under the terms of an April 2010 agreement with the Town of Meggett, the Commissioners provide 
wholesale wastewater transportation and treatment services to the Meggett area at a current rate of $3.19/Ccf.  CPW 
also provides retail wastewater billing and collection services for Meggett.  The Town of Meggett is responsible for 
the operation and maintenance of its wastewater collection system. 
THE CAPITAL IMPROVEMENTS PROGRAM 
The Capital Improvements Program (hereinafter, "CIP") consists of recommended master plan 
improvements and expansions to water and wastewater infrastructure for the years 2022 through 2027.  The CIP was 
developed by the staff of the Commissioners based upon the latest master planning undertaken by the staff and the 
Consulting Engineers.  The CIP was adopted by the Commissioners in 2021.  The CIP is designed to accommodate 
projected growth within the service area, address needs for continued regulatory compliance, and from an asset 
management perspective, includes substantial funds for rehabilitation and replacement of aging infrastructure. 
The construction schedule for the various improvements included in the CIP was determined on the basis of 
relative need and importance of each such improvement, the time required for planning and design work, and the 
extent to which modifications can be effected on existing facilities.  The CIP anticipates that a total of $310,389,000 
in improvements will be financed out of proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds and future revenue bonds, as well as 
from current and future revenues and funds of the System. 
The CIP contains $148,389,000 for major improvements to the water utility that includes expansion of 
capacity at the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant from 115.4 MGD to 127.4 MGD to meet projected peak day water 
demands; an aluminum sulfate (alum) residuals solar dryer facility to reduce or eliminate the risk of rapidly 
changing requirements and increasing fees for alum residuals disposal at landfills; transmission main extensions to 
help meet growth and fire flow demands in retail and wholesale service areas; and various water infrastructure 
relocation needs associated with road and drainage improvement projects.  The CIP also includes funding to 
purchase a raw water tunnel and property from INEOS in the Cainhoy area for the site of a future water treatment 
plant.  The CIP further includes improvements to the Hanahan Water Treatment Plant and to the water distribution 
system to ensure available capacity to meet water demands associated with growth and fire protection and to comply 
with a variety of increasing regulatory requirements. 
The CIP contains $157,000,000 for major improvements to the wastewater utility that includes a new 
effluent pump station at the Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant to discharge treated effluent during periods of 
peak flow and/or high tide events; a biosolids thermal dryer facility to reduce or eliminate the risk of rapidly 
changing requirements and increasing fees for biosolids disposal at landfills; extension of the West Ashley Sewer 
Tunnel to transport a projected buildout peak flow of 56 MGD from the West Ashley and John's Island service 
areas, and the service areas of wholesale customers Hollywood, Ravenel and Meggett; rehabilitation of collection 
system infrastructure; collection system extensions to help meet growth demands; and various sewer infrastructure 
relocation needs associated with road and drainage improvement projects.  The CIP further includes improvements 
to the Plum Island Wastewater Treatment Plant and to the wastewater collection system to ensure available capacity 
to handle projected growth-related wastewater flows and to comply with more stringent regulatory requirements. 
The CIP contains $5,000,000 for renovations to the Commissioners' St. Philip Street headquarters building 
that includes improvements to mechanical, electrical and roofing systems; lighting, audio-visual and information 
technology upgrades; and reconfiguration of work spaces, conference rooms and common areas.  These 
improvements will increase building efficiency and ensure the ability of the Commissioners to continue to serve 
customers from the St. Philip Street location. 31

Management's Discussion of Recent Operating Results  
In 2021, total assets increased by $18.33 million, or 0.97%, when compared to 2020 totals, while total 
liabilities decreased by $1 million, or 0.12%, over 2020.  Operating revenue in 2021 experienced an increase of $8.8 
million, or 5.6%, from fiscal year 2020.  Water and wastewater rates increased by 3% and 2.75%, respectively, in 
the 2021 fiscal year.  Wholesale water rates increased during the 2021 fiscal year.  Operating expenses increased by 
$53.5 thousand, or 0.04%, over 2020. 32 
Unaudited figures for 2022 through April 30, 2022 show an increase of $2.6 million, or 10.42%, in water 
sales and $1.8 million, or 8.29%, in wastewater sales compared to the same period in 2021.  At April 30, 2022, 
unaudited water and wastewater operating expenses were below budget projections by 26.5% and 20.9%, 
respectively.   
REPORT OF CONSULTING ENGINEERS 
The Report of the Consulting Engineers entitled "Bond Report – Waterworks and Sewer System Capital 
Improvement Revenue Bonds, Series 2022" issued on June 1, 2022 (the "2022 Report") sets forth the projected 
revenue and overall rate requirements of the water system and wastewater system components of the System for 
each of the six fiscal years from 2022 through 2027 (the "Study Period").  The following summarizes the 2022 
Report which is available by contacting Black & Veatch Corporation at whiteam@bv.com. 
The projections of operating results included in the 2022 Report are based on assumptions of future events.  
The assumptions were reviewed with and approved by the Commissioners and are based on circumstances and 
information available at the time the 2022 Report was prepared.  While the Consulting Engineers believe that the 
considerations and assumptions used constituted reasonable bases for the preparation of the projections, the 
achievement of the projected operating results is dependent upon the occurrence of future events that cannot be 
assured. 
Based on information reviewed, analyses performed and assumptions made with respect to the water and 
wastewater systems set forth in the 2022 Report, the Consulting Engineers concluded, in part, that the projected 
operating and capital program costs and bond coverage requirements can be financed during the Study Period, with 
revenue increases of 5% in each year from 2023 through 2027 for the water system, and 6% in each year from 2023 
through 2027 for the wastewater system.  Supporting cash flow analyses are presented in the following tables.
